     <p>The <b>University of Toronto</b> (<b>U of T</b>, <b>UToronto</b>, or <b>Toronto</b>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university" class="mw-redirect">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Toronto" title="Toronto">Toronto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ontario" title="Ontario">Ontario</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, situated on the grounds that surround <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_(Toronto)" title="Queen's Park (Toronto)">Queen's Park</a>. It was founded by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> in 1827 as <i>King's College</i>, the first institution of higher learning in <a href="/wiki/Upper_Canada" title="Upper Canada">Upper Canada</a>. Originally controlled by the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a>, the university assumed the present name in 1850 upon becoming a secular institution. As a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_university" title="Collegiate university">collegiate university</a>, it comprises twelve colleges that differ in character and history, each retaining substantial autonomy on financial and institutional affairs.</p> 
     <p>Academically, the University of Toronto is noted for influential movements and curricula in <a href="/wiki/Literary_criticism" title="Literary criticism">literary criticism</a> and <a href="/wiki/Communication_theory" title="Communication theory">communication theory</a>, known collectively as the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_School_of_communication_theory" title="Toronto School of communication theory">Toronto School</a>. The university was the birthplace of <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell</a> research, and was the site of the first practical <a href="/wiki/Electron_microscope" title="Electron microscope">electron microscope</a>, the development of <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">multi-touch</a> technology, the identification of <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_X-1" title="Cygnus X-1">Cygnus X-1</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">black hole</a>, and the theory of <a href="/wiki/NP_completeness" title="NP completeness" class="mw-redirect">NP completeness</a>. By a significant margin, it receives the most annual <a href="/wiki/Research_funding" title="Research funding" class="mw-redirect">research funding</a> of any Canadian university. It is one of two members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> located outside the United States.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Varsity_Blues" title="Toronto Varsity Blues">Varsity Blues</a> are the athletic teams representing the university in intercollegiate league matches, with particularly long and storied ties to <a href="/wiki/Gridiron_football" title="Gridiron football">gridiron football</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>. The university's <a href="/wiki/Hart_House_(University_of_Toronto)" title="Hart House (University of Toronto)">Hart House</a> is an early example of the North American <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student centre</a>, simultaneously serving cultural, intellectual and recreational interests within its large <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic-revival</a> complex.</p> 
     <p>The University of Toronto has educated two <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governors General</a> and four <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Ministers of Canada</a>, four foreign leaders, fourteen <a href="/wiki/List_of_Justices_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="List of Justices of the Supreme Court of Canada">Justices of the Supreme Court</a>, and has been affiliated with ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>. The university ranks 21st in the world in the <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a>, 27th in the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a>, and 19th in the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>.</p>

          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-8"><a href="#Athletics"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Athletics</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Culture_and_student_life"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Culture and student life</span></a> 
           <ul> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Greek_life"><span class="tocnumber">7.1</span> <span class="toctext">Greek life</span></a></li> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Theatre_and_music"><span class="tocnumber">7.2</span> <span class="toctext">Theatre and music</span></a></li> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Student_media"><span class="tocnumber">7.3</span> <span class="toctext">Student media</span></a></li> 
            <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Residences"><span class="tocnumber">7.4</span> <span class="toctext">Residences</span></a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-14"><a href="#Noted_people"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Noted people</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li> 
          <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li> 
         </ul> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The founding of a colonial college had long been the desire of <a href="/wiki/John_Graves_Simcoe" title="John Graves Simcoe">John Graves Simcoe</a>, the first <a href="/wiki/List_of_lieutenant_governors_of_Ontario" title="List of lieutenant governors of Ontario">Lieutenant-Governor of Upper Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-simcoeBiography_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-simcoeBiography-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_simcoe_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_simcoe-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> As an Oxford-educated military commander who had fought in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>, Simcoe believed a college was needed to counter the spread of <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">republicanism</a> from the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_simcoe_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_simcoe-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> The Upper Canada Executive Committee recommended in 1798 that a college be established in <a href="/wiki/York,_Upper_Canada" title="York, Upper Canada">York</a>, the colonial capital.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_simcoe_6-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_simcoe-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg/220px-UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg/330px-UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg/440px-UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UniversityCollegeUofT_1800s.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A painting by 
        <a href="/wiki/Byron_Edmund_Walker" title="Byron Edmund Walker">Sir Edmund Walker</a> depicts 
        <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Toronto" title="University College, Toronto">University College</a> as it appeared in 1858.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>On March 15, 1827, a <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> was formally issued by <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">King George IV</a>, proclaiming &quot;from this time one College, with the style and privileges of a University ... for the education of youth in the principles of the Christian Religion, and for their instruction in the various branches of Science and Literature ... to continue for ever, to be called King's College.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-charterStory_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charterStory-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> The granting of the charter was largely the result of intense lobbying by <a href="/wiki/John_Strachan" title="John Strachan">John Strachan</a>, the influential <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Canada" title="Anglican Church of Canada">Anglican</a> <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Toronto" title="Anglican Diocese of Toronto">Bishop of Toronto</a> who took office as the first president of the college.<sup id="cite_ref-charterStory_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charterStory-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The original three-storey <a href="/wiki/Greek_Revival_architecture" title="Greek Revival architecture">Greek Revival</a> school building was constructed on the present site of <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_(Toronto)" title="Queen's Park (Toronto)">Queen's Park</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_kingsCollege_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_kingsCollege-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Under Strachan's guidance, King's College was a religious institution that closely aligned with the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_England" title="Church of England">Church of England</a> and the British colonial elite, known as the <a href="/wiki/Family_Compact" title="Family Compact">Family Compact</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-strachanBiography_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-strachanBiography-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Reformist politicians opposed the clergy's control over colonial institutions and fought to have the college <a href="/wiki/Secularization" title="Secularization">secularized</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_secularization_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_secularization-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1849, after a lengthy and heated debate, the newly-elected <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a> of Upper Canada voted to rename King's College as the University of Toronto and severed the school's ties with the church.<sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Having anticipated this decision, the enraged Strachan had resigned a year earlier to open <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Toronto" title="Trinity College, Toronto">Trinity College</a> as a private Anglican seminary.<sup id="cite_ref-bfaught_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bfaught-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Toronto" title="University College, Toronto">University College</a> was created as the nondenominational teaching branch of the University of Toronto. During the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>, the threat of <a href="/wiki/Union_blockade" title="Union blockade">Union blockade</a> on <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> prompted the creation of the University Rifle Corps, which saw battle in resisting the <a href="/wiki/Fenian_raids" title="Fenian raids">Fenian raids</a> on the Niagara border in 1866.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_rifleCorps_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_rifleCorps-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg/220px-AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg/330px-AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a7/AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:AirplaneInFrontOfUC.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> A 
        <a href="/wiki/Sopwith_Camel" title="Sopwith Camel">Sopwith Camel</a> aircraft rests on the Front Campus lawn in 1918, during World War I.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Established in 1878, the School of Practical Science was precursor to the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Applied_Science_and_Engineering" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Applied Science and Engineering">Faculty of Applied Science and Engineering</a>, which has been nicknamed <i>Skule</i> since its earliest days.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_skule_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_skule-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> While the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Medicine" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Medicine">Faculty of Medicine</a> opened in 1843, medical teaching was conducted by proprietary schools from 1853 until 1887, when the faculty absorbed the Toronto School of Medicine.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_medicine_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_medicine-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Meanwhile, the university continued to set examinations and confer medical degrees during that period.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_medicine_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_medicine-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The university opened the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a> in 1887, and it was followed by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Dentistry" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Dentistry">Faculty of Dentistry</a> in 1888, when the <a href="/wiki/Royal_College_of_Dental_Surgeons_of_Ontario" title="Royal College of Dental Surgeons of Ontario">Royal College of Dental Surgeons</a> became an affiliate.<sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Women were admitted to the university for the first time in 1884.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_women_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_women-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>A devastating fire in 1890 gutted the interior of University College and destroyed thirty-three thousand volumes from the library,<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_fire_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_fire-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> but the university restored the building and replenished its library within two years.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_fire_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_fire-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Over the next two decades, a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_university" title="Collegiate university">collegiate system</a> gradually took shape as the university arranged federation with several ecclesiastical colleges, including Strachan's Trinity College in 1904. The university operated <a href="/wiki/The_Royal_Conservatory_of_Music" title="The Royal Conservatory of Music">the Royal Conservatory of Music</a> from 1896 to 1991 and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Ontario_Museum" title="Royal Ontario Museum">Royal Ontario Museum</a> from 1912 to 1968; both still retain close ties with the university as independent institutions.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Press" title="University of Toronto Press">University of Toronto Press</a> was founded in 1901 as the first <a href="/wiki/University_press" title="University press" class="mw-redirect">academic publishing house</a> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The Faculty of Forestry was established in 1907, with <a href="/wiki/Bernhard_Fernow" title="Bernhard Fernow">Bernhard Fernow</a> as founding dean; it was the first university faculty devoted to forest science in Canada. In 1910, the Faculty of Education opened its <a href="/wiki/Laboratory_school" title="Laboratory school">laboratory school</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Schools" title="University of Toronto Schools">University of Toronto Schools</a>. The <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">First</a> and <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World Wars</a> curtailed some university activities as undergraduate and graduate men eagerly enlisted.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_WWI_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_WWI-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_WWII_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_WWII-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Intercollegiate athletic competitions and the <a href="/wiki/Hart_House_Debating_Club" title="Hart House Debating Club" class="mw-redirect">Hart House Debates</a> were suspended, although exhibition and interfaculty games were still held.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_WWII_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_WWII-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/David_Dunlap_Observatory" title="David Dunlap Observatory">David Dunlap Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Hill,_Ontario" title="Richmond Hill, Ontario">Richmond Hill</a> opened in 1935, followed by the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Institute_for_Aerospace_Studies" title="University of Toronto Institute for Aerospace Studies">University of Toronto Institute for Aerospace Studies</a> in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> The university opened <a href="/wiki/Satellite_campus" title="Satellite campus">satellite campuses</a> in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Scarborough" title="University of Toronto Scarborough">Scarborough</a> in 1964 and in <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Mississauga" title="University of Toronto Mississauga">Mississauga</a> in 1967. The university's former affiliated schools at the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Agricultural_College" title="Ontario Agricultural College">Ontario Agricultural College</a> and <a href="/wiki/Glendon_College" title="Glendon College">Glendon Hall</a> became fully independent as <a href="/wiki/University_of_Guelph" title="University of Guelph">University of Guelph</a> in 1964 and <a href="/wiki/York_University" title="York University">York University</a> in 1965, respectively. Beginning in the 1980s, reductions in government funding prompted more rigorous fundraising efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Toronto was the first Canadian university to amass a <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">financial endowment</a> greater than C$1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Grounds">Grounds</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Grounds">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg/170px-WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg" width="170" height="226" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg/255px-WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg/340px-WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:WWTower-in-university-of-toronto_cropped.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Soldiers%27_Tower" title="Soldiers' Tower">Soldiers' Tower</a>, a memorial to alumni fallen in the World Wars, contains a 51-bell 
        <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The university grounds lie about 2 kilometres (1.2&nbsp;mi) north of the <a href="/wiki/Financial_District,_Toronto" title="Financial District, Toronto">Financial District</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Toronto" title="Downtown Toronto">Downtown Toronto</a>, and immediately south of the neighbourhoods of <a href="/wiki/Yorkville,_Toronto" title="Yorkville, Toronto">Yorkville</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Annex" title="The Annex">The Annex</a>. The site encompasses 71 hectares (180&nbsp;acres) bounded mostly by <a href="/wiki/Bay_Street" title="Bay Street">Bay Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bloor_Street" title="Bloor Street">Bloor Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spadina_Avenue" title="Spadina Avenue">Spadina Avenue</a> and <a href="/wiki/College_Street_(Toronto)" title="College Street (Toronto)">College Street</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-factsandfigures_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsandfigures-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> An enclave surrounded by university grounds, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_(Toronto)" title="Queen's Park (Toronto)">Queen's Park</a> contains the <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Legislative_Building" title="Ontario Legislative Building">Ontario Legislative Building</a> and several historic monuments. With its green spaces and many interlocking courtyards, the university forms a distinct region of <a href="/wiki/Urban_park" title="Urban park">urban parkland</a> in the city's downtown core.<sup id="cite_ref-openSpace_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-openSpace-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The namesake <a href="/wiki/University_Avenue_(Toronto)" title="University Avenue (Toronto)">University Avenue</a> is a ceremonial <a href="/wiki/Boulevard" title="Boulevard">boulevard</a> and arterial thoroughfare that runs through downtown between Queen's Park and <a href="/wiki/Front_Street_(Toronto)" title="Front Street (Toronto)">Front Street</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Spadina_(TTC)" title="Spadina (TTC)">Spadina</a>, <a href="/wiki/St._George_(TTC)" title="St. George (TTC)">St. George</a>, <a href="/wiki/Museum_(TTC)" title="Museum (TTC)">Museum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bay_(TTC)" title="Bay (TTC)">Bay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Park_(TTC)" title="Queen's Park (TTC)">Queen's Park</a> stations of the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_subway_and_RT" title="Toronto subway and RT">Toronto subway system</a> are located in the vicinity.</p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG/220px-Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG/330px-Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG/440px-Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Philosopher%27s_Walk.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Stone pillars of the Bennett Gates mark the southern entrance of 
        <a href="/wiki/Philosopher%27s_Walk_(Toronto)" title="Philosopher's Walk (Toronto)">Philosopher's Walk</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The architecture is defined by a combination of <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">Gothic Revival</a> buildings spread across the eastern and central portions of campus, most of them dating between 1858 and 1929. The traditional heart of the university, known as Front Campus, is located near the centre of the campus in an oval lawn enclosed by King's College Circle.<sup id="cite_ref-openSpace_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-openSpace-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The centrepiece is the main building of <a href="/wiki/University_College,_Toronto" title="University College, Toronto">University College</a>, built in 1857 with an eclectic blend of <a href="/wiki/Richardsonian_Romanesque" title="Richardsonian Romanesque">Richardsonian Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Norman_architecture" title="Norman architecture">Norman</a> architectural elements.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> The dramatic effect of this blended design by architect <a href="/wiki/Frederick_William_Cumberland" title="Frederick William Cumberland">Frederick William Cumberland</a> drew praise from European visitors of the time: &quot;Until I reached Toronto,&quot; remarked <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Hamilton-Temple-Blackwood,_1st_Marquess_of_Dufferin_and_Ava" title="Frederick Hamilton-Temple-Blackwood, 1st Marquess of Dufferin and Ava">Lord Dufferin</a> during his visit in 1872, &quot;I confess I was not aware that so magnificent a specimen of architecture existed upon the American continent.&quot;<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> The building was declared a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada" title="National Historic Sites of Canada">National Historic Site of Canada</a> in 1968.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup> Built in 1907, <a href="/wiki/Convocation_Hall_(University_of_Toronto)" title="Convocation Hall (University of Toronto)">Convocation Hall</a> is recognizable for its domed roof and <a href="/wiki/Ionic_order" title="Ionic order">Ionic</a>-pillared rotunda. Although its foremost function is hosting the annual convocation ceremonies, the building serves as a venue for academic and social events throughout the year.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> The sandstone buildings of <a href="/wiki/Knox_College,_Toronto" title="Knox College, Toronto">Knox College</a> epitomizes the North American <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_Gothic_in_North_America" title="Collegiate Gothic in North America">collegiate Gothic</a> design, with its characteristic cloisters surrounding a secluded courtyard.<sup id="cite_ref-fraser1995_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fraser1995-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uoft_conhall-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Uoft_conhall-2.jpg/220px-Uoft_conhall-2.jpg" width="220" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Uoft_conhall-2.jpg/330px-Uoft_conhall-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Uoft_conhall-2.jpg/440px-Uoft_conhall-2.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uoft_conhall-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The neoclassical 
        <a href="/wiki/Convocation_Hall_(University_of_Toronto)" title="Convocation Hall (University of Toronto)">Convocation Hall</a> is characterized by its domed roof and 
        <a href="/wiki/Ionic_order" title="Ionic order">Ionic</a>-pillared rotunda.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>A lawn at the northeast is anchored by <a href="/wiki/Hart_House_(University_of_Toronto)" title="Hart House (University of Toronto)">Hart House</a>, a Gothic-revival <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student centre</a> complex. Among its many common rooms, the building's Great Hall is noted for large stained-glass windows and a long quotation from <a href="/wiki/John_Milton" title="John Milton">John Milton</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Areopagitica" title="Areopagitica">Areopagitica</a></i> that is inscribed around the walls.<sup id="cite_ref-kilgour_1999_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kilgour_1999-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup> The adjacent <a href="/wiki/Soldiers%27_Tower" title="Soldiers' Tower">Soldiers' Tower</a> stands 143 feet (44&nbsp;m) tall as the most prominent structure in the vicinity, its stone arches etched with the names of university members lost to the battlefields of the two World Wars.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The tower houses a 51-bell <a href="/wiki/Carillon" title="Carillon">carillon</a> that is played on special occasions such as <a href="/wiki/Remembrance_Day" title="Remembrance Day">Remembrance Day</a> and convocation.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> The oldest surviving building on campus is the former <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Magnetic_and_Meteorological_Observatory" title="Toronto Magnetic and Meteorological Observatory">Toronto Magnetic and Meteorological Observatory</a> building, built in 1855.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup> North of University College, the main building of <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Toronto" title="Trinity College, Toronto">Trinity College</a> displays <a href="/wiki/Jacobethan" title="Jacobethan">Jacobethan</a> <a href="/wiki/Tudor_architecture" title="Tudor architecture">Tudor</a> architecture, while its chapel was built in the <a href="/wiki/Perpendicular_Gothic" title="Perpendicular Gothic" class="mw-redirect">Perpendicular Gothic</a> style of <a href="/wiki/Giles_Gilbert_Scott" title="Giles Gilbert Scott">Giles Gilbert Scott</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> The chapel features exterior walls of sandstone and interiors of <a href="/wiki/Indiana_Limestone" title="Indiana Limestone">Indiana Limestone</a>, and was constructed by Italian stonemasons using ancient building methods.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Philosopher%27s_Walk_(Toronto)" title="Philosopher's Walk (Toronto)">Philosopher's Walk</a> is a scenic footpath that follows a meandering, wooded <a href="/wiki/Ravine" title="Ravine">ravine</a> linking with Trinity College, <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Arena" title="Varsity Arena">Varsity Arena</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a>. <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University,_Toronto" title="Victoria University, Toronto">Victoria College</a> is on the eastern side of Queen's Park, centred on a Romanesque main building made of contrasting red sandstone and grey limestone.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Developed after the Second World War, the western section of the campus consists mainly of <a href="/wiki/Modern_architecture" title="Modern architecture">modernist</a> and <a href="/wiki/International_Style_(architecture)" title="International Style (architecture)">internationalist</a> structures that contain laboratories and faculty offices.<sup id="cite_ref-openSpace_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-openSpace-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> The most significant example of <a href="/wiki/Brutalist_architecture" title="Brutalist architecture">Brutalist architecture</a> is the massive <a href="/wiki/Robarts_Library" title="Robarts Library">Robarts Library</a> complex, built in 1972 and opened a year later in 1973. It features raised podia, extensive use of triangular geometric designs and a towering fourteen-storey concrete structure that cantilevers above a field of open space and mature trees.<sup id="cite_ref-mcClelland_2007_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcClelland_2007-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> The library is undergoing renovations to increase indoor space. The <a href="/wiki/Leslie_L._Dan_Pharmacy_Building" title="Leslie L. Dan Pharmacy Building" class="mw-redirect">Leslie L. Dan Pharmacy Building</a>, completed in 2006, exhibits a modern style of glass and steel by British architect <a href="/wiki/Norman_Foster,_Baron_Foster_of_Thames_Bank" title="Norman Foster, Baron Foster of Thames Bank">Norman Foster</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance_and_colleges">Governance and colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Governance and colleges">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_College.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Victoria_College.jpg/220px-Victoria_College.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Victoria_College.jpg/330px-Victoria_College.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/80/Victoria_College.jpg/440px-Victoria_College.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Victoria_College.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Old Vic, the main building of 
        <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University,_Toronto" title="Victoria University, Toronto">Victoria College</a>, typifies the 
        <a href="/wiki/Richardsonian_Romanesque" title="Richardsonian Romanesque">Richardsonian Romanesque</a> style.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The University of Toronto has traditionally been a decentralized institution, with governing authority shared among its central administration, academic faculties and colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-ross1972_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ross1972-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The Governing Council is the <a href="/wiki/Unicameral" title="Unicameral" class="mw-redirect">unicameral</a> legislative organ of the central administration, overseeing general academic, business and institutional affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-uoftAct_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uoftAct-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> Before 1971, the university was governed under a <a href="/wiki/Bicameral" title="Bicameral" class="mw-redirect">bicameral</a> system composed of the board of governors and the university senate.<sup id="cite_ref-ross1972_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ross1972-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> The chancellor, usually a former <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">governor general</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Ontario" title="Lieutenant Governor of Ontario">lieutenant governor</a>, premier or diplomat, is the ceremonial head of the university. The president is appointed by the council as the chief executive.<sup id="cite_ref-uoftAct_42-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uoftAct-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Unlike most North American institutions, the University of Toronto is a <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_university" title="Collegiate university">collegiate university</a> with a model that resembles those of the University of Cambridge and the University of Oxford in Britain.<sup id="cite_ref-alexander1906_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexander1906-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The colleges hold substantial autonomy over admissions, scholarships, programs and other academic and financial affairs, in addition to the housing and social duties of typical <a href="/wiki/Residential_college" title="Residential college">residential colleges</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uoftAct_42-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uoftAct-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-alexander1906_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexander1906-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The system emerged in the 19th century, as ecclesiastical colleges considered various forms of union with the University of Toronto to ensure their viability. The desire to preserve religious traditions in a secular institution resulted in the federative collegiate model that came to characterize the university.<sup id="cite_ref-alexander1906_43-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alexander1906-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Trinity_chapel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Trinity_chapel.jpg/170px-Trinity_chapel.jpg" width="170" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Trinity_chapel.jpg/255px-Trinity_chapel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Trinity_chapel.jpg/340px-Trinity_chapel.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Trinity_chapel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Chapel of 
        <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Toronto" title="Trinity College, Toronto">Trinity College</a> reflects the college's Anglican heritage.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/University_College,_Toronto" title="University College, Toronto">University College</a> was the founding nondenominational college, created in 1853 after the university was secularized. <a href="/wiki/Knox_College,_Toronto" title="Knox College, Toronto">Knox College</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian</a> institution, and <a href="/wiki/Wycliffe_College" title="Wycliffe College" class="mw-redirect">Wycliffe College</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Low_church" title="Low church">low church</a> seminary, both encouraged their students to study for non-divinity degrees at University College.<sup id="cite_ref-torontoBaptistCollege_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torontoBaptistCollege-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1885, they entered a formal affiliation with the University of Toronto, and became <a href="/wiki/Federated_school" title="Federated school" class="mw-redirect">federated schools</a> in 1890.<sup id="cite_ref-fraser1995_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fraser1995-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> The idea of federation initially met strong opposition at <a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_in_the_University_of_Toronto" title="Victoria University in the University of Toronto" class="mw-redirect">Victoria University</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodist</a> school in <a href="/wiki/Cobourg,_Ontario" title="Cobourg, Ontario">Cobourg</a>, but a financial incentive in 1890 convinced the school to join.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_victoriaCollege_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_victoriaCollege-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Decades after the death of John Strachan, the Anglican seminary <a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Toronto" title="Trinity College, Toronto">Trinity College</a> entered federation in 1904,<sup id="cite_ref-trinityHistory_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trinityHistory-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> followed in 1910 by <a href="/wiki/St._Michael%27s_College,_Toronto" title="St. Michael's College, Toronto">St. Michael's College</a>, a Roman Catholic college founded by the <a href="/wiki/Basilian_Fathers" title="Basilian Fathers" class="mw-redirect">Basilian Fathers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-stMichaelsHistory_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stMichaelsHistory-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> Among the institutions that had considered federation but ultimately remained independent were <a href="/wiki/McMaster_University" title="McMaster University">McMaster University</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">Baptist</a> school that later moved to <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_Ontario" title="Hamilton, Ontario">Hamilton</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-torontoBaptistCollege_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-torontoBaptistCollege-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> and Queen's College, a Presbyterian school in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston</a> that later became <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen's University">Queen's University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <table style="float:right; border:1px solid #ddd; background:#fefefe; padding:3px; margin:5px; width:33%;"> 
      <caption style="font-size: 100%">
       <b>Colleges of the University of Toronto</b>
      </caption> 
      <tbody>
       <tr style="vertical-align:top; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"> 
        <td style="width:50%;"> <p><b>Constituent colleges</b></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Innis_College,_Toronto" title="Innis College, Toronto">Innis College</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/New_College,_Toronto" title="New College, Toronto">New College</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/University_College,_Toronto" title="University College, Toronto">University College</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Woodsworth_College,_Toronto" title="Woodsworth College, Toronto">Woodsworth College</a></li> 
         </ul> <p><b>Theological colleges</b></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Knox_College,_Toronto" title="Knox College, Toronto">Knox College</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Regis_College,_Toronto" title="Regis College, Toronto">Regis College</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Wycliffe_College,_Toronto" title="Wycliffe College, Toronto">Wycliffe College</a></li> 
         </ul> </td> 
        <td> <p><b>Federated colleges</b></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/St._Michael%27s_College,_Toronto" title="St. Michael's College, Toronto">St. Michael's College</a></li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Trinity_College,_Toronto" title="Trinity College, Toronto">Trinity College</a> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/St._Hilda%27s_College,_University_of_Toronto" title="St. Hilda's College, University of Toronto">St. Hilda's College</a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Victoria_University_in_the_University_of_Toronto" title="Victoria University in the University of Toronto" class="mw-redirect">Victoria University</a> 
           <ul> 
            <li><a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_College,_Toronto" title="Emmanuel College, Toronto">Emmanuel College</a></li> 
           </ul> </li> 
         </ul> <p><b>Postgraduate college</b></p> 
         <ul> 
          <li><a href="/wiki/Massey_College,_Toronto" title="Massey College, Toronto">Massey College</a></li> 
         </ul> </td> 
       </tr> 
      </tbody>
     </table> 
     <p>The post-war era saw the creation of <a href="/wiki/New_College,_Toronto" title="New College, Toronto">New College</a> in 1962, <a href="/wiki/Innis_College,_Toronto" title="Innis College, Toronto">Innis College</a> in 1964 and <a href="/wiki/Woodsworth_College" title="Woodsworth College" class="mw-redirect">Woodsworth College</a> in 1974, all of them nondenominational.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Along with University College, they comprise the university's constituent colleges, which are established and funded by the central administration and are therefore financially dependent.<sup id="cite_ref-finances_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finances-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-1974memorandum_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1974memorandum-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Massey_College,_Toronto" title="Massey College, Toronto">Massey College</a> was established in 1963 by the <a href="/wiki/Massey_Foundation" title="Massey Foundation">Massey Foundation</a> as a college exclusively for graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Regis_College,_Toronto" title="Regis College, Toronto">Regis College</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Jesuit" title="Jesuit" class="mw-redirect">Jesuit</a> seminary, entered federation with the university in 1979.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>In contrast with the constituent colleges, the colleges of Knox, Massey, Regis, St. Michael's, Trinity, Victoria and Wycliffe continue to exist as legally distinct entities, each possessing a separate <a href="/wiki/Financial_endowment" title="Financial endowment">financial endowment</a>. While St. Michael's, Trinity and Victoria continue to recognize their religious affiliations and heritage, they have since adopted secular policies of enrolment and teaching in non-divinity subjects.<sup id="cite_ref-1974memorandum_52-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1974memorandum-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Some colleges have, or once had, collegiate structures of their own: <a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_College,_Toronto" title="Emmanuel College, Toronto">Emmanuel College</a> is a college of Victoria and <a href="/wiki/St._Hilda%27s_College,_University_of_Toronto" title="St. Hilda's College, University of Toronto">St. Hilda's College</a> is part of Trinity;<sup id="cite_ref-trinityHistory_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-trinityHistory-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup> St. Joseph?s College had existed as a college within St. Michael's until it was dissolved in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-stMichaelsHistory_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stMichaelsHistory-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ewart_College" title="Ewart College">Ewart College</a> existed as an affiliated college until 1991, when it was merged into Knox College.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> Postgraduate theology degrees are conferred by the colleges of Knox, Regis and Wycliffe, along with the divinity faculties within Emmanuel, St. Michael's and Trinity, including joint degrees with the university through the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_School_of_Theology" title="Toronto School of Theology">Toronto School of Theology</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG/220px-Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG/330px-Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/81/Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG/440px-Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Munk_Centre_for_International_Studies.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Munk_School_of_Global_Affairs" title="Munk School of Global Affairs">Munk School of Global Affairs</a> encompasses programs and research institutes for international relations.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Arts_and_Science" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Arts and Science">Faculty of Arts and Science</a> is the university's main undergraduate faculty, and administers most of the courses in the college system.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> While the colleges are not entirely responsible for teaching duties, most of them house specialized academic programs and lecture series. Among other subjects, Trinity College is associated with programs in <a href="/wiki/International_relations" title="International relations">international relations</a>, as are University College with <a href="/wiki/Canadian_studies" title="Canadian studies">Canadian studies</a>, Victoria College with <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> studies, Innis College with <a href="/wiki/Film_studies" title="Film studies">film studies</a>, New College with <a href="/wiki/Gender_studies" title="Gender studies">gender studies</a>, Woodsworth College with <a href="/wiki/Industrial_relations" title="Industrial relations">industrial relations</a> and St. Michael's College with <a href="/wiki/Medievalism" title="Medievalism">Medievalism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Applied_Science_and_Engineering" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Applied Science and Engineering">Faculty of Applied Science and Engineering</a> is the other major faculty that allows direct-entry into bachelor's degree programs from secondary schools; undergraduate programs in other faculties generally admit by <a href="/wiki/Second_entry_degree" title="Second entry degree">second entry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the average entry grades from Ontario secondary schools were 85.8% for the arts, 88.4% for sciences, 90.0% for business and 90.1% for engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-t2011_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-t2011-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> Postgraduate programs in arts and science are administered by the School of Graduate Studies.</p> 
     <p>The University of Toronto is the birthplace of an influential <a href="/wiki/School_of_thought" title="School of thought">school of thought</a> on <a href="/wiki/Communication_theory" title="Communication theory">communication theory</a> and <a href="/wiki/Literary_criticism" title="Literary criticism">literary criticism</a>, known as the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_School_of_communication_theory" title="Toronto School of communication theory">Toronto School</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-alphabetEffect_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alphabetEffect-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-worldOnPaper_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-worldOnPaper-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wordIsMightierThanThePen_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordIsMightierThanThePen-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> Described as &quot;the theory of the primacy of communication in the structuring of human cultures and the structuring of the human mind&quot;,<sup id="cite_ref-wordIsMightierThanThePen_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wordIsMightierThanThePen-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> the school is rooted in the works of <a href="/wiki/Eric_A._Havelock" title="Eric A. Havelock">Eric A. Havelock</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harold_Innis" title="Harold Innis">Harold Innis</a> and the subsequent contributions of <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Snow_Carpenter" title="Edmund Snow Carpenter">Edmund Snow Carpenter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Frye" title="Northrop Frye">Northrop Frye</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_McLuhan" title="Marshall McLuhan">Marshall McLuhan</a>. Since 1963, the <a href="/wiki/McLuhan_Program_in_Culture_and_Technology" title="McLuhan Program in Culture and Technology">McLuhan Program in Culture and Technology</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Information" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Information">Faculty of Information</a> has carried the mandate for teaching and advancing the Toronto School.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Uoft_SF-01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Uoft_SF-01.jpg/220px-Uoft_SF-01.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Uoft_SF-01.jpg/330px-Uoft_SF-01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Uoft_SF-01.jpg/440px-Uoft_SF-01.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Uoft_SF-01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/Sandford_Fleming" title="Sandford Fleming">Sandford Fleming</a> Building contains offices of the 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Applied_Science_and_Engineering" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Applied Science and Engineering">Faculty of Applied Science and Engineering</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Several notable works in arts and humanities are based at the university, including the <i><a href="/wiki/Dictionary_of_Canadian_Biography" title="Dictionary of Canadian Biography">Dictionary of Canadian Biography</a></i> since 1959 and the <i>Collected Works of <a href="/wiki/Desiderius_Erasmus" title="Desiderius Erasmus">Erasmus</a></i> since 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Records_of_Early_English_Drama" title="Records of Early English Drama" class="mw-redirect">Records of Early English Drama</a></i> collects and edits the surviving documentary evidence of dramatic arts in pre-<a href="/wiki/Puritan" title="Puritan">Puritan</a> England,<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> while the <i><a href="/wiki/Dictionary_of_Old_English" title="Dictionary of Old English">Dictionary of Old English</a></i> compiles the early vocabulary of the English language from the Anglo-Saxon period.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Munk_School_of_Global_Affairs" title="Munk School of Global Affairs">Munk School of Global Affairs</a> encompasses the university's various programs and curricula in international affairs and foreign policy. As the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a> heightened, Toronto's <a href="/wiki/Slavic_studies" title="Slavic studies">Slavic studies</a> program evolved into an important institution on Soviet politics and economics, financed by the <a href="/wiki/Rockefeller_Foundation" title="Rockefeller Foundation">Rockefeller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ford_Foundation" title="Ford Foundation">Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andrew_W._Mellon_Foundation" title="Andrew W. Mellon Foundation">Mellon</a> foundations.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> The Munk School is also home to the <a href="/wiki/G20_Research_Group" title="G20 Research Group">G20 Research Group</a>, which conducts independent monitoring and analysis on the <a href="/wiki/G-20_major_economies" title="G-20 major economies">Group of Twenty</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Lab" title="Citizen Lab">Citizen Lab</a>, which conducts research on <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship" title="Internet censorship">Internet censorship</a> as a joint founder of the <a href="/wiki/OpenNet_Initiative" title="OpenNet Initiative">OpenNet Initiative</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The university operates international offices in Berlin, Hong Kong and <a href="/wiki/Siena" title="Siena">Siena</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Medicine" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Medicine">Faculty of Medicine</a> is affiliated with a network of ten <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospitals</a>, providing medical treatment, research and advisory services to patients and clients from Canada and abroad.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> A core member of the network is <a href="/wiki/University_Health_Network" title="University Health Network">University Health Network</a>, itself a specialized federation of <a href="/wiki/Toronto_General_Hospital" title="Toronto General Hospital">Toronto General Hospital</a>, <a href="/wiki/Princess_Margaret_Cancer_Centre" title="Princess Margaret Cancer Centre">Princess Margaret Cancer Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Western_Hospital" title="Toronto Western Hospital">Toronto Western Hospital</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Rehabilitation_Institute" title="Toronto Rehabilitation Institute">Toronto Rehabilitation Institute</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Physicians in the medical institutes have cross-appointments to faculty and supervisory positions in university departments. The <a href="/wiki/Rotman_School_of_Management" title="Rotman School of Management">Rotman School of Management</a> developed the discipline and methodology of <a href="/wiki/Integrative_thinking" title="Integrative thinking">integrative thinking</a>, upon which the school bases its curriculum.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Founded in 1887, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a>'s emphasis on formal teachings of <a href="/wiki/Liberal_arts_education" title="Liberal arts education">liberal arts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Legal_theory" title="Legal theory" class="mw-redirect">legal theory</a> was then considered unconventional, but gradually helped shift the country's legal education system away from the apprenticeship model that prevailed until the mid-20th century.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Ontario_Institute_for_Studies_in_Education" title="Ontario Institute for Studies in Education">Ontario Institute for Studies in Education</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Teachers_college" title="Teachers college" class="mw-redirect">teachers college</a> of the university, affiliated with its two <a href="/wiki/Laboratory_school" title="Laboratory school">laboratory schools</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_Child_Study" title="Institute of Child Study">Institute of Child Study</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Schools" title="University of Toronto Schools">University of Toronto Schools</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> Autonomous institutes at the university include the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Institute_for_Theoretical_Astrophysics" title="Canadian Institute for Theoretical Astrophysics">Canadian Institute for Theoretical Astrophysics</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Pontifical_Institute_of_Mediaeval_Studies" title="Pontifical Institute of Mediaeval Studies">Pontifical Institute of Mediaeval Studies</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fields_Institute" title="Fields Institute">Fields Institute</a>.</p> 
     <table style="border:1px solid #ddd; background:#fefefe; padding:3px; margin:0; margin:auto;">

     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Library_and_collections">Library and collections</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Library and collections">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Robartslibrary4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Robartslibrary4.jpg/220px-Robartslibrary4.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Robartslibrary4.jpg/330px-Robartslibrary4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Robartslibrary4.jpg/440px-Robartslibrary4.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Robartslibrary4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Robarts_Library" title="Robarts Library">Robarts Library</a> houses the university's main collection for humanities and social sciences.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Libraries" title="University of Toronto Libraries">University of Toronto Libraries</a> is the fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/Academic_library" title="Academic library">academic library</a> system in North America, following those of <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University_Library" title="Harvard University Library">Harvard</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yale_University_Library" title="Yale University Library">Yale</a> and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Illinois_at_Urbana%E2%80%93Champaign" title="University of Illinois at Urbana?Champaign">Illinois</a>, measured by number of volumes held.<sup id="cite_ref-arl2007-08_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arl2007-08-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> The collections include more than 10 million bound volumes, 5.4 million <a href="/wiki/Microfilm" title="Microfilm" class="mw-redirect">microfilms</a>, 70,000 serial titles and 1 million maps, films, graphics and sound recordings.<sup id="cite_ref-libraryStatistics_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libraryStatistics-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The largest of the libraries, <a href="/wiki/Robarts_Library" title="Robarts Library">Robarts Library</a>, holds about five million bound volumes that form the main collection for <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a> and <a href="/wiki/Social_science" title="Social science">social sciences</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Fisher_Rare_Book_Library" title="Thomas Fisher Rare Book Library">Thomas Fisher Rare Book Library</a> constitutes one of the largest repositories of publicly accessible <a href="/wiki/Book_collecting" title="Book collecting">rare books</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manuscript" title="Manuscript">manuscripts</a>. Its collections range from ancient Egyptian <a href="/wiki/Papyrus" title="Papyrus">papyri</a> to <a href="/wiki/Incunable" title="Incunable">incunabula</a> and <a href="/wiki/Libretto" title="Libretto">libretti</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> the subjects of focus include British, <a href="/wiki/European_literature" title="European literature">European</a> and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_literature" title="Canadian literature">Canadian literature</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aristotle" title="Aristotle">Aristotle</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_Darwin" title="Charles Darwin">Darwin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science" title="History of science">history of science</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_medicine" title="History of medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canadiana" title="Canadiana">Canadiana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_books" title="History of books">history of books</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Most of the remaining holdings are dispersed at departmental and faculty libraries, in addition to about 1.3 million bound volumes that are held by the colleges.<sup id="cite_ref-libraryStatistics_80-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-libraryStatistics-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has collaborated with the <a href="/wiki/Internet_Archive" title="Internet Archive">Internet Archive</a> since 2005 to <a href="/wiki/Digitizing" title="Digitizing">digitize</a> some of its library holdings.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Housed within University College, the University of Toronto Art Centre contains three major art collections. The Malcove Collection is primarily represented by <a href="/wiki/Early_Christianity" title="Early Christianity">Early Christian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine</a> sculptures, bronzeware, furniture, icons and liturgical items.<sup id="cite_ref-malcove_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malcove-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> It also includes glassware and stone reliefs from the <a href="/wiki/Greco-Roman_world" title="Greco-Roman world">Greco-Roman</a> period, and the painting <i><a href="/wiki/Adam_and_Eve" title="Adam and Eve">Adam and Eve</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Lucas_Cranach_the_Elder" title="Lucas Cranach the Elder">Lucas Cranach the Elder</a>, dated from 1538.<sup id="cite_ref-malcove_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-malcove-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The University of Toronto Collection features <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_Canadian_art" title="Contemporary Canadian art">Canadian contemporary art</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-uoft-ucCollection_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uoft-ucCollection-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> while the University College Art Collection holds significant works by the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven_(artists)" title="Group of Seven (artists)">Group of Seven</a> and 19th century <a href="/wiki/Landscape_art" title="Landscape art">landscape artists</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-uoft-ucCollection_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-uoft-ucCollection-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation">Reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Reputation">edit</a>]</span></h3>

        <th scope="row" style="text-align:left;"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">THE-WUR</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_93-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup></th> 
        <td>1</td> 
       </tr> 
       <tr> 
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:right;"> 
         <div class="noprint plainlinks hlist navbar mini" style=""> 
          <ul> 
           <li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template:Canadian university rankings"><span title="View this template" style="">v</span></a></li> 
           <li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Canadian_university_rankings" title="Template talk:Canadian university rankings"><span title="Discuss this template" style="">t</span></a></li> 
           <li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Canadian_university_rankings&amp;action=edit"><span title="Edit this template" style="">e</span></a></li> 
          </ul> 
         </div> </td> 
       </tr>
