     </table> 
     <p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a></i> of 2012 ranks the University of Toronto at 21st place globally and 1st in Canada, and 16th place globally based on reputation,<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_93-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> while the <i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a></i> of 2012 place the university at 19th in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> In the <i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a></i> of 2012, the University of Toronto is placed at 27th in the world and 1st in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-arwu_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-arwu-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> It ranked 25th worldwide in the 2012 report compiled by <i><a href="/wiki/Human_Resources_%26_Labor_Review" title="Human Resources &amp; Labor Review" class="mw-redirect">Human Resources &amp; Labor Review</a></i> on graduate performance,<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> 9th worldwide in the 2010 <a href="/wiki/Performance_Ranking_of_Scientific_Papers_for_World_Universities" title="Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities">Performance Ranking of Scientific Papers for World Universities</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-prspwu_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-prspwu-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> 14th in the <a href="/wiki/High_Impact_Universities" title="High Impact Universities">High Impact Universities</a> ranking,<sup id="cite_ref-hiu_107-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hiu-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup> 49th in a <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">New York Times</a></i> employment survey in 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> and 2nd globally in the <a href="/wiki/University_Ranking_by_Academic_Performance" title="University Ranking by Academic Performance" class="mw-redirect">University Ranking by Academic Performance</a> of 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-URAP2012_109-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-URAP2012-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the university received a grade of A- for environmental sustainability from the Sustainable Endowments Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-The_College_Sustainability_Report_Card_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_College_Sustainability_Report_Card-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> The university has placed first among Canada's research universities in the annual ranking by Research Infosource since 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-researchInfosource2012_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchInfosource2012-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, the University of Toronto was named by <i><a href="/wiki/Newsweek" title="Newsweek">Newsweek</a></i> as one of the top three schools outside of the United States.<sup id="cite_ref-Newsweek_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Newsweek-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Toronto ranked as the nation's top medical-doctoral university in <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean's">Maclean's</a></i> magazine for eleven consecutive years between 1994 and 2004.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> Since 2009, it has joined 22 other national institutions in withholding data from the magazine, citing continued concerns regarding methodology.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2010, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Faculty_of_Law" title="University of Toronto Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a> was named the top law school in Canada by <i>Maclean's</i> for the fourth consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>Since 1926, the University of Toronto has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a>, a consortium of the leading North American research universities. The university manages by far the largest annual <a href="/wiki/Research_funding" title="Research funding" class="mw-redirect">research budget</a> of any university in Canada, with sponsored direct-cost expenditures of $878.725 million in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-researchInfosource2012_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchInfosource2012-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-researchReport2006_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchReport2006-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-researchReport2007_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchReport2007-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> The federal government was the largest source of funding, with grants from the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Institutes_of_Health_Research" title="Canadian Institutes of Health Research">Canadian Institutes of Health Research</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Natural_Sciences_and_Engineering_Research_Council" title="Natural Sciences and Engineering Research Council">Natural Sciences and Engineering Research Council</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Social_Sciences_and_Humanities_Research_Council" title="Social Sciences and Humanities Research Council">Social Sciences and Humanities Research Council</a> amounting to about one-third of the research budget. About 8 percent of research funding came from corporations, mostly in the <a href="/wiki/Health_care_industry" title="Health care industry">health care industry</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-researchReport2007_117-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchReport2007-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Humanstemcell.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Humanstemcell.JPG/220px-Humanstemcell.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Humanstemcell.JPG/330px-Humanstemcell.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Humanstemcell.JPG/440px-Humanstemcell.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Humanstemcell.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The discovery of 
        <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cells</a> by 
        <a href="/wiki/Ernest_McCulloch" title="Ernest McCulloch">McCulloch</a> and 
        <a href="/wiki/James_Till" title="James Till">Till</a> is the basis for all modern stem cell research.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The first practical <a href="/wiki/Electron_microscope" title="Electron microscope">electron microscope</a> was built by the physics department in 1938.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> During World War II, the university developed the <a href="/wiki/G-suit" title="G-suit">G-suit</a>, a life-saving garment worn by Allied fighter plane pilots, later adopted for use by astronauts.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Development of the <a href="/wiki/Infrared" title="Infrared">infrared</a> <a href="/wiki/Chemiluminescence" title="Chemiluminescence">chemiluminescence</a> technique improved analyses of energy behaviours in chemical reactions.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1963, the asteroid <a href="/wiki/2104_Toronto" title="2104 Toronto">2104 Toronto</a> is discovered in the <a href="/wiki/David_Dunlap_Observatory" title="David Dunlap Observatory">David Dunlap Observatory</a> in <a href="/wiki/Richmond_Hill,_Ontario" title="Richmond Hill, Ontario">Richmond Hill</a> and is named after the university.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1972, studies on <a href="/wiki/Cygnus_X-1" title="Cygnus X-1">Cygnus X-1</a> led to the publication of the first observational evidence proving the existence of <a href="/wiki/Black_hole" title="Black hole">black holes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> Toronto astronomers have also discovered the <a href="/wiki/Uranus" title="Uranus">Uranus</a> moons of <a href="/wiki/Caliban_(moon)" title="Caliban (moon)">Caliban</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sycorax_(moon)" title="Sycorax (moon)">Sycorax</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Dwarf_galaxy" title="Dwarf galaxy">dwarf galaxies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andromeda_I" title="Andromeda I">Andromeda I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andromeda_II" title="Andromeda II">II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andromeda_III" title="Andromeda III">III</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Supernova" title="Supernova">supernova</a> <a href="/wiki/SN_1987A" title="SN 1987A">SN 1987A</a>. A pioneer in computing technology, the university designed and built <a href="/wiki/UTEC" title="UTEC">UTEC</a>, one of the world's first operational computers, and later purchased <i>Ferut</i>, the second commercial computer after <a href="/wiki/UNIVAC_I" title="UNIVAC I">UNIVAC I</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Multi-touch" title="Multi-touch">Multi-touch</a> technology was developed at Toronto, with applications ranging from <a href="/wiki/Mobile_device" title="Mobile device">handheld devices</a> to <a href="/wiki/Multi-Touch_Collaboration_Wall" title="Multi-Touch Collaboration Wall">collaboration walls</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg/220px-Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg/330px-Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg/440px-Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Doors_Unlocked_and_Open_May_2011.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The Donnelly Centre is part of the 
        <a href="/wiki/Discovery_District" title="Discovery District">Discovery District</a>, one of the world's largest biotechnology research clusters.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>The discovery of <a href="/wiki/Insulin" title="Insulin">insulin</a> at the University of Toronto in 1921 is considered among the most significant events in the <a href="/wiki/History_of_medicine" title="History of medicine">history of medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Stem_cell" title="Stem cell">stem cell</a> was discovered at the university in 1963, forming the basis for <a href="/wiki/Hematopoietic_stem_cell_transplantation" title="Hematopoietic stem cell transplantation">bone marrow transplantation</a> and all subsequent research on <a href="/wiki/Adult_stem_cell" title="Adult stem cell">adult</a> and <a href="/wiki/Embryonic_stem_cell" title="Embryonic stem cell">embryonic stem cells</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> This was the first of many findings at Toronto relating to stem cells, including the identification of <a href="/wiki/Pancreas" title="Pancreas">pancreatic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Retina" title="Retina">retinal</a> stem cells.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Cancer_stem_cell" title="Cancer stem cell">cancer stem cell</a> was first identified in 1997 by Toronto researchers,<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> who have since found stem cell associations in <a href="/wiki/Leukemia" title="Leukemia">leukemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brain_tumor" title="Brain tumor">brain tumors</a> and <a href="/wiki/Colorectal_cancer" title="Colorectal cancer">colorectal cancer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Medical inventions developed at Toronto include the <a href="/wiki/Glycemic_index" title="Glycemic index">glycaemic index</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> the infant cereal <a href="/wiki/Pablum" title="Pablum">Pablum</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> the use of protective <a href="/wiki/Hypothermia" title="Hypothermia">hypothermia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Open_heart_surgery" title="Open heart surgery" class="mw-redirect">open heart surgery</a><sup id="cite_ref-pearce_2005_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pearce_2005-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> and the first <a href="/wiki/Artificial_cardiac_pacemaker" title="Artificial cardiac pacemaker">artificial cardiac pacemaker</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-pearce_2005_138-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-pearce_2005-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> The first successful <a href="/wiki/Lung_transplantation" title="Lung transplantation">single-lung transplant</a> was performed at Toronto in 1981, followed by the first <a href="/wiki/Nerve" title="Nerve">nerve</a> transplant in 1988,<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> and the first double-lung transplant in 1989. Researchers identified the <a href="/wiki/Maturation_promoting_factor" title="Maturation promoting factor">maturation promoting factor</a> that regulates <a href="/wiki/Cell_division" title="Cell division">cell division</a>, and discovered the <a href="/wiki/T-cell_receptor" title="T-cell receptor">T-cell receptor</a> which trigger responses of the immune system.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup> The university is credited with isolating the genes that cause <a href="/wiki/Fanconi_anemia" title="Fanconi anemia">Fanconi anemia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cystic_fibrosis" title="Cystic fibrosis">cystic fibrosis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Early-onset_Alzheimer%27s_disease" title="Early-onset Alzheimer's disease">early-onset Alzheimer's disease</a>, among numerous other diseases.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup> Between 1914 and 1972, the university operated the <a href="/wiki/Connaught_Medical_Research_Laboratories" title="Connaught Medical Research Laboratories" class="mw-redirect">Connaught Medical Research Laboratories</a>, now part of the pharmaceutical corporation <a href="/wiki/Sanofi-Aventis" title="Sanofi-Aventis" class="mw-redirect">Sanofi-Aventis</a>. Among the research conducted at the laboratory was the development of <a href="/wiki/Gel_electrophoresis" title="Gel electrophoresis">gel electrophoresis</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The University of Toronto is the primary research presence that supports one of the world's largest concentrations of <a href="/wiki/Biotechnology" title="Biotechnology">biotechnology</a> firms.<sup id="cite_ref-kleiner_2008_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kleiner_2008-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> More than 5,000 <a href="/wiki/Principal_investigator" title="Principal investigator">principal investigators</a> reside within 2&nbsp;kilometres from the university grounds in Toronto's <a href="/wiki/Discovery_District" title="Discovery District">Discovery District</a>, conducting $1 billion of medical research annually.<sup id="cite_ref-kleiner_2008_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kleiner_2008-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/MaRS_Discovery_District" title="MaRS Discovery District">MaRS Discovery District</a> is a <a href="/wiki/Research_park" title="Research park">research park</a> that serves commercial enterprises and the university's <a href="/wiki/Technology_transfer" title="Technology transfer">technology transfer</a> ventures. In 2008, the university disclosed 159 inventions and had 114 active start-up companies.<sup id="cite_ref-factsandfigures_4-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsandfigures-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Its <a href="/wiki/SciNet_Consortium" title="SciNet Consortium">SciNet Consortium</a> operates the most powerful <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">supercomputer</a> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <p>The 44 sports teams of the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Varsity_Blues" title="Toronto Varsity Blues">Varsity Blues</a> represent the university in intercollegiate competitions. The two main leagues in which the Blues participate are <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Interuniversity_Sport" title="Canadian Interuniversity Sport">Canadian Interuniversity Sport</a> for national competitions, and the auxiliary <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> conference at the provincial level. The <a href="/wiki/Athletic_nickname" title="Athletic nickname">athletic nickname</a> of Varsity Blues was not consistently used until the 1930s; previously, references such as &quot;Varsity&quot;, &quot;The Big Blue&quot;, &quot;The Blue and White&quot; and &quot;The Varsity Blue&quot; also appeared interchangeably.<sup id="cite_ref-footballMediaGuide2008_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footballMediaGuide2008-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>The Blue and White</i> is commonly played and sung in athletic games as a <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Toronto_varsity_rowing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Toronto_varsity_rowing.jpg/290px-Toronto_varsity_rowing.jpg" width="290" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Toronto_varsity_rowing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e1/Toronto_varsity_rowing.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Toronto_varsity_rowing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> The 
        <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Rowing_Club" title="University of Toronto Rowing Club">University of Toronto Rowing Club</a> trains in 
        <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Harbour" title="Toronto Harbour">Toronto Harbour</a> for the 
        <a href="/wiki/1924_Summer_Olympics" title="1924 Summer Olympics">1924 Summer Olympics</a>. The team won silver for Canada.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Gridiron_football" title="Gridiron football">North American football</a> traces its very origin to the University of Toronto, with the first documented football game played at University College on November 9, 1861.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> The Blues played their first intercollegiate football match in 1877 against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Michigan" title="University of Michigan">University of Michigan</a>, in a game that ended with a scoreless draw.<sup id="cite_ref-footballMediaGuide2008_145-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footballMediaGuide2008-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> Since intercollegiate seasons began in 1898, the Blues have won four <a href="/wiki/Grey_Cup" title="Grey Cup">Grey Cup</a>, two <a href="/wiki/Vanier_Cup" title="Vanier Cup">Vanier Cup</a> and 25 <a href="/wiki/Yates_Cup" title="Yates Cup">Yates Cup</a> championships, including the inaugural championships for all three trophies.<sup id="cite_ref-footballMediaGuide2008_145-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-footballMediaGuide2008-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the football team has hit a rough patch following its last championship in 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup> From 2001 until 2008, the Blues suffered the longest <a href="/wiki/Losing_streak_(sport)" title="Losing streak (sport)" class="mw-redirect">losing streak</a> in Canadian collegiate history, recording 49 consecutive winless games.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup> This was preceded by a single victory in 2001 that ended a run of 18 straight losses.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> The site of <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Stadium" title="Varsity Stadium">Varsity Stadium</a> has served as the primary playing grounds of the Varsity Blues football and soccer programs since 1898.<sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Formed in 1891, the storied <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Varsity_Blues_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Toronto Varsity Blues men's ice hockey">Varsity Blues men's ice hockey team</a> has left many legacies on the national, professional and international hockey scenes. <a href="/wiki/Conn_Smythe" title="Conn Smythe">Conn Smythe</a> played for the Blues as a <a href="/wiki/Centre_(ice_hockey)" title="Centre (ice hockey)">centre</a> during his undergraduate years, and was a Blues coach from 1923 to 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-mensHockeyBrochure2008_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mensHockeyBrochure2008-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> When Smythe took over the <a href="/wiki/Toronto_Maple_Leafs" title="Toronto Maple Leafs">Toronto Maple Leafs</a> in 1927, the familiar blue-and-white sweater design of the Varsity Blues was adopted by his new team.<sup id="cite_ref-mensHockeyBrochure2008_152-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mensHockeyBrochure2008-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Blues hockey competed at the <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey_at_the_1928_Winter_Olympics" title="Ice hockey at the 1928 Winter Olympics">1928 Winter Olympics</a> and captured the gold medal for Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> At the <a href="/wiki/1980_Winter_Olympics" title="1980 Winter Olympics">1980 Winter Olympics</a>, Blues coach <a href="/wiki/Tom_Watt" title="Tom Watt">Tom Watt</a> served as co-coach of the Canadian hockey team in which six players were Varsity grads.<sup id="cite_ref-mensHockeyBrochure2008_152-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mensHockeyBrochure2008-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> In all, the Blues have won the <a href="/wiki/CIS_University_Cup" title="CIS University Cup">CIS University Cup</a> national hockey title ten times, last in 1984. <a href="/wiki/Varsity_Arena" title="Varsity Arena">Varsity Arena</a> has been the permanent home of the Blues ice hockey programs since it opened in 1926.<sup id="cite_ref-friedland_2002_8-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-friedland_2002-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> In men's basketball, the Varsity Blues have won 14 conference titles, including the inaugural championship in 1909, but have not won a national title.<sup id="cite_ref-mensBasketball2008_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mensBasketball2008-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup> In swimming, the men's team has claimed the national crown 16 times since 1964, while the women's team has claimed the crown 14 times since 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Established in 1897, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Rowing_Club" title="University of Toronto Rowing Club">University of Toronto Rowing Club</a> is the oldest collegiate <a href="/wiki/Rowing_club" title="Rowing club">rowing club</a> in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-bluesBeforeSunrise_156-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bluesBeforeSunrise-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup> It earned a silver medal for the country in the <a href="/wiki/1924_Summer_Olympics" title="1924 Summer Olympics">1924 Summer Olympics</a>, finishing second to Yale's crew.<sup id="cite_ref-bluesBeforeSunrise_156-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bluesBeforeSunrise-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture_and_student_life">Culture and student life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture and student life">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tleft"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg/220px-Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg" width="220" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg/330px-Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg/440px-Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Toronto_-_ON_-_Hart_House.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Generations of students have attended speeches, debates and concerts at 
        <a href="/wiki/Hart_House_(University_of_Toronto)" title="Hart House (University of Toronto)">Hart House</a>.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>In the heart of social, cultural and recreational life at the University of Toronto lies <a href="/wiki/Hart_House_(University_of_Toronto)" title="Hart House (University of Toronto)">Hart House</a>, the sprawling <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Revival_architecture" title="Gothic Revival architecture">neo-Gothic</a> <a href="/wiki/Student_activity_center" title="Student activity center">student activity centre</a> that was conceived by alumnus-benefactor <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Massey" title="Vincent Massey">Vincent Massey</a> and named for his grandfather <a href="/wiki/Hart_Massey" title="Hart Massey">Hart</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> Opened in 1919, the complex established a communitarian spirit in the university and its students, who at the time kept largely within their own colleges under the decentralized collegiate system.<sup id="cite_ref-faught_house_158-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faught_house-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup> At Hart House, a student can read in the library, dine casually or formally, have a haircut,<sup id="cite_ref-hair_place_hart_house_159-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hair_place_hart_house-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> visit the art gallery, watch a play in the theatre, listen to a concert, observe or join in debates, play billiards, or go for a swim and find a place to study, all under the same roof and within the span of a day. The confluence of assorted functions is the result of a deliberate effort to create a holistic educational experience, a goal summarized in the Founders' Prayer.<sup id="cite_ref-faught_house_158-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faught_house-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup> The Hart House model was influential in the planning of student centres at other universities, notably <a href="/wiki/Cornell_University" title="Cornell University">Cornell University</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Willard_Straight_Hall" title="Willard Straight Hall">Willard Straight Hall</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Hart House resembles some traditional aspects of student representation through its financial support of student clubs, and its standing committees and board of stewards that are composed mostly of undergraduate students. However, the main <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students' union">students' unions</a> on administrative and policy issues are the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto_Students%27_Union" title="University of Toronto Students' Union">University of Toronto Students' Union</a>, Association of Part-time Undergraduate Students and the Graduate Students' Union. Student representative bodies also exist at the various colleges, academic faculties and departments.</p> 
     <p>The <a href="/wiki/Hart_House_Debating_Club" title="Hart House Debating Club" class="mw-redirect">Hart House Debating Club</a> employs a <a href="/wiki/Debate" title="Debate">debating</a> style that combines the American emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Analysis" title="Analysis">analysis</a> and the British use of <a href="/wiki/Wit" title="Wit">wit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-webb_fightingWords_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webb_fightingWords-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> Smaller debating societies at Trinity, University and Victoria College have served as initial training grounds for debaters who later progress to Hart House.<sup id="cite_ref-webb_fightingWords_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-webb_fightingWords-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup> The club won the <a href="/wiki/World_Universities_Debating_Championship" title="World Universities Debating Championship">World Universities Debating Championship</a> in 1981 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup> University of Toronto Model United Nations (UTMUN) hosts an annual <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a> conference in Toronto, while the United Nations Society participates in various North American and international conferences.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> The Toronto chess team has captured the top title six times at the <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_Intercollegiate_Team_Chess_Championship" title="Pan American Intercollegiate Team Chess Championship">Pan American Intercollegiate Team Chess Championship</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Formula_SAE" title="Formula SAE">Formula SAE</a> Racing Team won the Formula Student European Championships in 2003, 2005 and 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Greek_life">Greek life</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Greek life">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <p>The University of Toronto is home to the first <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_Canada" title="Fraternities and sororities in Canada">collegiate fraternity in Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi</a>, whose Toronto chapter has been active since 1879.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup> Because few other Canadian universities in the 19th century were deemed comparable to their American counterparts in repute, age and secularity, most early American fraternities chose to open their first international chapter at the University of Toronto, including <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Upsilon" title="Delta Upsilon">Delta Upsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Delta_Theta" title="Phi Delta Theta">Phi Delta Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Sigma" title="Phi Kappa Sigma">Phi Kappa Sigma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phi_Gamma_Delta" title="Phi Gamma Delta">Phi Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Delta Kappa Epsilon">Delta Kappa Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Psi_Upsilon" title="Psi Upsilon">Psi Upsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Beta_Theta_Pi" title="Beta Theta Pi">Beta Theta Pi</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Phi_Kappa_Pi&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Phi Kappa Pi (page does not exist)">Phi Kappa Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Phi_Epsilon" title="Lambda Phi Epsilon">Lambda Phi Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Nu" title="Sigma Nu">Sigma Nu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Theta_Delta_Chi" title="Theta Delta Chi">Theta Delta Chi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omicron_Pi" title="Alpha Omicron Pi">Alpha Omicron Pi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Delta_Delta" title="Delta Delta Delta">Delta Delta Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Kappa_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Kappa Delta Phi">Alpha Kappa Delta Phi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Lambda_Chi_Alpha" title="Lambda Chi Alpha">Lambda Chi Alpha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup> Other Greek-letter societies include <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Delta" title="Alpha Gamma Delta">Alpha Gamma Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Society" title="Kappa Alpha Society">Kappa Alpha Society</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pi_Beta_Phi" title="Pi Beta Phi">Pi Beta Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Pi" title="Sigma Pi">Sigma Pi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>. A <a href="/wiki/Collegiate_secret_societies_in_North_America" title="Collegiate secret societies in North America">secret society</a> known as <i><a href="/wiki/Episkopon" title="Episkopon">Episkopon</a></i> has operated from Trinity College since 1858.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Theatre_and_music">Theatre and music</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Theatre and music">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg/220px-Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg/330px-Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg/440px-Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Skule_Choir_imgp8938.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Sunlight fills 
        <a href="/wiki/Knox_College,_Toronto" title="Knox College, Toronto">Knox College Chapel</a> during a Christmas concert of the engineering faculty's Skule Choir.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><a href="/wiki/Hart_House_Theatre" title="Hart House Theatre">Hart House Theatre</a> is the university's student <a href="/wiki/Amateur_theatre" title="Amateur theatre">amateur theatre</a>, generally producing four major plays every season. As old as Hart House itself, the theatre is considered a pioneer in <a href="/wiki/Theatre_of_Canada" title="Theatre of Canada">Canadian theatre</a> for introducing the <a href="/wiki/Little_Theatre_Movement" title="Little Theatre Movement">Little Theatre Movement</a> from Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup> It has cultivated numerous performing-arts talents, including <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sutherland" title="Donald Sutherland">Donald Sutherland</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lorne_Michaels" title="Lorne Michaels">Lorne Michaels</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wayne_and_Shuster" title="Wayne and Shuster">Wayne and Shuster</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Hutt_(actor)" title="William Hutt (actor)">William Hutt</a>. Three members of the <a href="/wiki/Group_of_Seven_(artists)" title="Group of Seven (artists)">Group of Seven</a> artists (<a href="/wiki/Lawren_Harris" title="Lawren Harris">Harris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Lismer" title="Arthur Lismer">Lismer</a> and <a href="/wiki/J._E._H._MacDonald" title="J. E. H. MacDonald">MacDonald</a>) have been set designers at the theatre,<sup id="cite_ref-hhtheatre_172-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hhtheatre-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> and composer <a href="/wiki/Healey_Willan" title="Healey Willan">Healey Willan</a> was director of music for fourteen productions.<sup id="cite_ref-hhtheatre_172-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hhtheatre-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup> The theatre also hosts annual variety shows run by several student theatrical companies at the colleges and academic faculties, the most prominent of which are <i>U.C. Follies</i> of University College, <i>Skule Nite</i> of the Faculty of Engineering, and <i>Daffydil</i> of the Faculty of Medicine, the latter in its hundredth year of production in 2010?2011.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>The main musical ensembles at Hart House are the orchestra, the chamber strings, the chorus, the jazz choir, the jazz ensemble and the symphonic band. The <i>Jazz at Oscar's</i> concert series performs <a href="/wiki/Big_band" title="Big band">big band</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vocal_jazz" title="Vocal jazz">vocal jazz</a> on Friday nights at the period lounge and bar of the Hart House Arbor Room.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Open Stage</i> is the monthly <a href="/wiki/Open_mic" title="Open mic">open mic</a> event featuring singers, comics, poets and storytellers. The Sunday Concert is the oldest musical series at Hart House; since 1922 the series has performed more than 600 classical music concerts in the Great Hall, freely attended by the university community and general audiences.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup> The public may also screen midday events held at noon, when concerts are recited prior to formal debut.</p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_media">Student media</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Student media">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:UndergradKingStudying.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/UndergradKingStudying.jpg/220px-UndergradKingStudying.jpg" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/UndergradKingStudying.jpg/330px-UndergradKingStudying.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/UndergradKingStudying.jpg/440px-UndergradKingStudying.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:UndergradKingStudying.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a> was active in student media during his undergraduate years.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Varsity_(newspaper)" title="The Varsity (newspaper)">The Varsity</a></i> is one of Canada's oldest student-run newspapers, in publication since 1880.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_women_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_women-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> The paper was originally a daily broadsheet, but has since adopted a compact format and is now weekly with three summer issues. <i>Hart House Review</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Literary_magazine" title="Literary magazine">literary magazine</a> by students of the Literary and Library Committee of Hart House, features prose, poetry, art and photography from emerging writers and artists. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Newspaper" title="The Newspaper">The Newspaper</a></i> is an independent student-run community newspaper, published weekly since 1978. <a href="/wiki/CIUT-FM" title="CIUT-FM">CIUT-FM</a> is the university's <a href="/wiki/Campus_radio" title="Campus radio">campus radio</a> station, while the University of Toronto Television broadcasts student-produced content. Students at each college and academic faculty also produce their own set of journals and news publications. University College's <a href="/wiki/The_Gargoyle_(newspaper)" title="The Gargoyle (newspaper)">The Gargoyle</a> was an early training ground for such notables as journalist Naomi Klein, and musician/comedian Paul Shaffer.</p> 
     <p>Members of the student press have contributed to activist causes on several notable occasions. At the height of debate on coeducation in 1880, <i>The Varsity</i> published an article in its inaugural issue voicing in favour of admitting women.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_women_16-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_women-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1895, the university suspended the editor of <i>The Varsity</i> for breach of collegiality, after he published a letter that harshly criticized the provincial government's dismissal of a professor and involvement in academic affairs. University College students then approved a motion by <i>Varsity</i> staff member <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a> and boycotted lectures for a week.<sup id="cite_ref-historyQA_king_177-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-historyQA_king-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178"><span>[</span>178<span>]</span></a></sup> After Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Trudeau" title="Pierre Trudeau">Pierre Trudeau</a> decriminalized homosexuality in 1969, a medical research assistant placed an advertisement in <i>The Varsity</i> seeking volunteers to establish the first university homophile association in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179"><span>[</span>179<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Residences">Residences</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Residences">edit</a>]</span></h3> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Teefy_Hall.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Teefy_Hall.JPG/220px-Teefy_Hall.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Teefy_Hall.JPG/330px-Teefy_Hall.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Teefy_Hall.JPG/440px-Teefy_Hall.JPG 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Teefy_Hall.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> Teefy House, a residence hall of 
        <a href="/wiki/St._Michael%27s_College,_Toronto" title="St. Michael's College, Toronto">St. Michael's College</a>, is home to senior undergraduate students.
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <p>Each college at the University of Toronto operates its own set of <a href="/wiki/Residence_hall" title="Residence hall" class="mw-redirect">residence halls</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cafeteria" title="Cafeteria">dining halls</a> clustered in a different area of the campus. Innis, New, St. Michael's, Trinity, University, Victoria, and Woodsworth colleges reserve most of their dormitories for their undergraduate students within the Faculty of Arts and Science, while setting a portion available to students from the professional and postgraduate faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180"><span>[</span>180<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Massey_College,_Toronto" title="Massey College, Toronto">Massey College</a> is exclusively for graduate students, while Knox and Wycliffe Colleges mainly house graduate theology students. <a href="/wiki/Annesley_Hall" title="Annesley Hall">Annesley Hall</a> of Victoria College, a <a href="/wiki/National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada" title="National Historic Sites of Canada">National Historic Site</a>, was the first university residence for women in Canada. After <a href="/wiki/St._Hilda%27s_College,_University_of_Toronto" title="St. Hilda's College, University of Toronto">St. Hilda's College</a> became coeducational in 2005, Annesley Hall and Loretto College of St. Michael's College are the last remaining women's halls at the university.</p> 
     <p>As campus residences accommodate just 6,400 students in all, the university guarantees housing only for undergraduates in their first year of study, while most upper-year and graduate students reside off-campus.<sup id="cite_ref-factsandfigures_4-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-factsandfigures-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181"><span>[</span>181<span>]</span></a></sup> Traditionally, the adjacent neighbourhoods of <a href="/wiki/The_Annex" title="The Annex">The Annex</a> and <a href="/wiki/Harbord_Village" title="Harbord Village">Harbord Village</a> are popular settling grounds for University of Toronto students, forming a distinct <a href="/wiki/Student_quarter" title="Student quarter">student quarter</a> enclave.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182"><span>[</span>182<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2004, the university purchased and converted a nearby hotel into the <a href="/wiki/Chestnut_Residence" title="Chestnut Residence">Chestnut Residence</a>, which houses students from all colleges and faculties. There are also numerous fraternity houses and <a href="/wiki/Student_housing_cooperative" title="Student housing cooperative">student housing cooperatives</a>, where boarders pay reduced rent for assuming housekeeping duties.</p> 
     <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Noted_people">Noted people</span><span class="mw-editsection">[<a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Toronto&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Noted people">edit</a>]</span></h2> 
     <div class="thumb tright"> 
      <div class="thumbinner" style="width:112px;">
       <a href="/wiki/File:Frederick_Banting_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Frederick_Banting_%282%29.jpg/110px-Frederick_Banting_%282%29.jpg" width="110" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Frederick_Banting_%282%29.jpg/165px-Frederick_Banting_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a6/Frederick_Banting_%282%29.jpg 2x" /></a> 
       <div class="thumbcaption"> 
        <div class="magnify">
         <a href="/wiki/File:Frederick_Banting_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"><img src="//bits.wikimedia.org/static-1.22wmf8/skins/common/images/magnify-clip.png" width="15" height="11" alt="" /></a>
        </div> 
        <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Banting" title="Frederick Banting">Sir Frederick Banting</a> (1891?1941): M.B. 1916, M.D. 1922, medical faculty 1922?41
       </div> 
      </div> 
     </div> 
     <div class="rellink relarticle mainarticle">
      Main article: 
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Toronto_people" title="List of University of Toronto people">List of University of Toronto people</a>
     </div> 
     <p>In addition to <a href="/wiki/Eric_A._Havelock" title="Eric A. Havelock">Havelock</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Innis" title="Harold Innis">Innis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northrop_Frye" title="Northrop Frye">Frye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Edmund_Snow_Carpenter" title="Edmund Snow Carpenter">Carpenter</a> and <a href="/wiki/Marshall_McLuhan" title="Marshall McLuhan">McLuhan</a>, former professors of the past century include <a href="/wiki/Frederick_Banting" title="Frederick Banting">Frederick Banting</a>, <a href="/wiki/Harold_Scott_MacDonald_Coxeter" title="Harold Scott MacDonald Coxeter">Harold Scott MacDonald Coxeter</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robertson_Davies" title="Robertson Davies">Robertson Davies</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_Charles_Fields" title="John Charles Fields">John Charles Fields</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leopold_Infeld" title="Leopold Infeld">Leopold Infeld</a> and <a href="/wiki/C._B._Macpherson" title="C. B. Macpherson">C. B. Macpherson</a>. Ten <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a> studied or taught at the University of Toronto. As of 2006, University of Toronto academics accounted for 15 of 23 Canadian members in the <a href="/wiki/American_Academy_of_Arts_and_Sciences" title="American Academy of Arts and Sciences">American Academy of Arts and Sciences</a> (65%) and 20 of 72 Canadian fellows in the <a href="/wiki/American_Association_for_the_Advancement_of_Science" title="American Association for the Advancement of Science">American Association for the Advancement of Science</a> (28%).<sup id="cite_ref-researchReport2006_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchReport2006-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> Among honorees from Canada between 1980 and 2006, University of Toronto faculty made up 11 of 21 <a href="/wiki/Gairdner_Foundation_International_Award" title="Gairdner Foundation International Award">Gairdner Foundation International Award</a> recipients (52%), 44 of 101 <a href="/wiki/Guggenheim_Fellowship" title="Guggenheim Fellowship">Guggenheim Fellows</a> (44%), 16 of 38 <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society" title="Royal Society">Royal Society</a> fellows (42%), 10 of 28 members in the <a href="/wiki/United_States_National_Academies" title="United States National Academies">United States National Academies</a> (36%) and 23 of 77 <a href="/wiki/Sloan_Research_Fellow" title="Sloan Research Fellow" class="mw-redirect">Sloan Research Fellows</a> (30%).<sup id="cite_ref-researchReport2006_116-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-researchReport2006-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup></p> 
     <p>Alumni of the University of Toronto's colleges, faculties and professional schools have assumed notable roles in a wide range of fields and specialties. In government, <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governors General</a> <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Massey" title="Vincent Massey">Vincent Massey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adrienne_Clarkson" title="Adrienne Clarkson">Adrienne Clarkson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Ministers</a> <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Meighen" title="Arthur Meighen">Arthur Meighen</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lester_B._Pearson" title="Lester B. Pearson">Lester B. Pearson</a> and <a href="/wiki/Paul_Martin" title="Paul Martin">Paul Martin</a>, and 14 <a href="/wiki/List_of_Justices_of_the_Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="List of Justices of the Supreme Court of Canada">Justices of the Supreme Court</a> have all graduated from the university, while world leaders include <a href="/wiki/President_of_Latvia" title="President of Latvia">President of Latvia</a> <a href="/wiki/Vaira_V%C4%AB%C4%B7e-Freiberga" title="Vaira V??e-Freiberga">Vaira V??e-Freiberga</a>, <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_the_Republic_of_China" title="Premier of the Republic of China">Premier of the Republic of China</a> <a href="/wiki/Liu_Chao-shiuan" title="Liu Chao-shiuan">Liu Chao-shiuan</a> and <a href="/wiki/President_of_Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="President of Trinidad and Tobago">President of Trinidad and Tobago</a> <a href="/wiki/Noor_Hassanali" title="Noor Hassanali">Noor Hassanali</a>. Economist <a href="/wiki/John_Kenneth_Galbraith" title="John Kenneth Galbraith">John Kenneth Galbraith</a>, political scientist <a href="/wiki/David_Easton" title="David Easton">David Easton</a>, historian <a href="/wiki/Margaret_MacMillan" title="Margaret MacMillan">Margaret MacMillan</a>, philosophers <a href="/wiki/David_Gauthier" title="David Gauthier">David Gauthier</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ted_Honderich" title="Ted Honderich">Ted Honderich</a>, anthropologist <a href="/wiki/Davidson_Black" title="Davidson Black">Davidson Black</a>, social activist <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Pence" title="Ellen Pence">Ellen Pence</a>, sociologist <a href="/wiki/Erving_Goffman" title="Erving Goffman">Erving Goffman</a>, psychologists <a href="/wiki/Endel_Tulving" title="Endel Tulving">Endel Tulving</a>, <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Schacter" title="Daniel Schacter">Daniel Schacter</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lisa_Feldman_Barrett" title="Lisa Feldman Barrett">Lisa Feldman Barrett</a>, physicians <a href="/wiki/Norman_Bethune" title="Norman Bethune">Norman Bethune</a> and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Herbert_Best" title="Charles Herbert Best">Charles Best</a>, geologists <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Tyrrell" title="Joseph Tyrrell">Joseph Tyrrell</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Tuzo_Wilson" title="John Tuzo Wilson">John Tuzo Wilson</a>, mathematicians <a href="/wiki/Irving_Kaplansky" title="Irving Kaplansky">Irving Kaplansky</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Kahan" title="William Kahan">William Kahan</a>, physicists <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Leonard_Schawlow" title="Arthur Leonard Schawlow">Arthur Leonard Schawlow</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bertram_Brockhouse" title="Bertram Brockhouse">Bertram Brockhouse</a>, architect <a href="/wiki/James_Strutt" title="James Strutt">James W. Strutt</a>, engineer <a href="/wiki/Gerald_Bull" title="Gerald Bull">Gerald Bull</a>, computer scientists <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Aho" title="Alfred Aho">Alfred Aho</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Kernighan" title="Brian Kernighan">Brian Kernighan</a>, astronauts <a href="/wiki/Roberta_Bondar" title="Roberta Bondar">Roberta Bondar</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julie_Payette" title="Julie Payette">Julie Payette</a> are also some of the most well-known academic figures from the university.</p> 
     <p>In business, University of Toronto alumni include <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Communications" title="Rogers Communications">Rogers Communications</a>' <a href="/wiki/Edward_Samuel_Rogers" title="Edward Samuel Rogers">Ted Rogers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Toronto-Dominion_Bank" title="Toronto-Dominion Bank">Toronto-Dominion Bank</a>'s <a href="/wiki/W._Edmund_Clark" title="W. Edmund Clark">W. Edmund Clark</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bank_of_Montreal" title="Bank of Montreal">Bank of Montreal</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Bill_Downe" title="Bill Downe">Bill Downe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scotiabank" title="Scotiabank">Scotiabank</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Peter_Godsoe" title="Peter Godsoe">Peter Godsoe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barrick_Gold" title="Barrick Gold">Barrick Gold</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Peter_Munk" title="Peter Munk">Peter Munk</a>, <a href="/wiki/BlackBerry_(company)" title="BlackBerry (company)">BlackBerry's</a> <a href="/wiki/Jim_Balsillie" title="Jim Balsillie">Jim Balsillie</a>, <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Jeffrey_Skoll" title="Jeffrey Skoll">Jeffrey Skoll</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fiat" title="Fiat">Fiat S.p.A.</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Marchionne" title="Sergio Marchionne">Sergio Marchionne</a>. In literature and media, the university has produced writers <a href="/wiki/Stephen_Leacock" title="Stephen Leacock">Stephen Leacock</a>, <a href="/wiki/John_McCrae" title="John McCrae">John McCrae</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rohinton_Mistry" title="Rohinton Mistry">Rohinton Mistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Atwood" title="Margaret Atwood">Margaret Atwood</a> and <a href="/wiki/Michael_Ondaatje" title="Michael Ondaatje">Michael Ondaatje</a>, film directors <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Hiller" title="Arthur Hiller">Arthur Hiller</a>, <a href="/wiki/Norman_Jewison" title="Norman Jewison">Norman Jewison</a>, <a href="/wiki/David_Cronenberg" title="David Cronenberg">David Cronenberg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atom_Egoyan" title="Atom Egoyan">Atom Egoyan</a>, actor <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sutherland" title="Donald Sutherland">Donald Sutherland</a>, screenwriter <a href="/wiki/David_Shore" title="David Shore">David Shore</a>, television producer and writer <a href="/wiki/Hart_Hanson" title="Hart Hanson">Hart Hanson</a>, musician <a href="/wiki/Paul_Shaffer" title="Paul Shaffer">Paul Shaffer</a>, journalists <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Gladwell" title="Malcolm Gladwell">Malcolm Gladwell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Klein" title="Naomi Klein">Naomi Klein</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Amiel" title="Barbara Amiel">Barbara Amiel</a>.</p>

(2005). <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.ca/books?id=zAdhk7aI2fAC&amp;lpg=PP1&amp;dq=Minerva's%20Aviary%3A%20Philosophy%20at%20Toronto&amp;pg=PP1#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true">Minerva's Aviary: Philosophy at Toronto</a></i>. University of Toronto Press. <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0802038700" class="internal mw-magiclink-isbn">ISBN 0-8020-3870-0</a>.</li> 
       <li>Wallace, W. Stewart. <i>A History of the University of Toronto, 1827?1927.</i> University of Toronto Press, 1927.</li> 
      </ul> 
     </div>
